- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls

# Cross-Compiler Sanitizer Tracing: ASan in LLVM vs GCC

## Your Task

AddressSanitizer (ASan) is implemented in both LLVM and GCC. Find the key source files that implement ASan instrumentation in each compiler. In `llvm/llvm-project`: 1. The C++ source file under `compiler-rt/lib/asan/` that implements ASan interceptors for standard library functions. 2. The C++ source file under `compiler-rt/lib/asan/` that implements the ASan runtime initialization. 3. The LLVM pass that inserts ASan instrumentation at the IR level (look for `AddressSanitizer` in `llvm/lib/Transforms/Instrumentation/`). In `gcc-mirror/gcc`: 4. The C++ source file that implements ASan instrumentation in GCC (`gcc/asan.cc`). 5. The header file for ASan in GCC (`gcc/asan.h`). Report the repo, file path, and primary class or function name for each file.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `github.com/llvm/llvm-project` (llvm/llvm-project)
- `github.com/gcc-mirror/gcc` (gcc-mirror/gcc)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

Perfect! I've completed the analysis and created the answer.json file. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Key ASan Implementation Files Found

### LLVM/LLVM-Project
1. **compiler-rt/lib/asan/asan_interceptors.cpp** - Intercepts standard library functions (malloc, free, pthread operations) using the INTERCEPTOR macro pattern
2. **compiler-rt/lib/asan/asan_rtl.cpp** - Contains `__asan_init()` function that initializes the ASan runtime when the program starts
3. **llvm/lib/Transforms/Instrumentation/AddressSanitizer.cpp** - Contains `AddressSanitizerPass` (main pass) and `AddressSanitizer` struct (function-level instrumentation) that inserts IR-level checks

### GCC-Mirror/GCC  
4. **gcc/asan.cc** - Contains `asan_instrument()` function and `pass_asan` class that implement GIMPLE-level instrumentation
5. **gcc/asan.h** - Header declaring the public ASan API (asan_function_start, asan_finish_file, asan_protect_global, etc.)

## Instrumentation Architecture

Both compilers follow a similar pattern:
- **LLVM**: Instruments at the IR level through the AddressSanitizerPass
- **GCC**: Instruments at the GIMPLE level through the pass_asan optimization pass

Both systems add shadow memory checks before memory operations and initialize via startup functions (`__asan_init` in LLVM's runtime, called through module constructors in GCC).

The answer file has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete file paths, symbols, and detailed explanations.

ASan Interceptors (compiler-rt/lib/asan/asan_interceptors.cpp)**\\n- Implements interception of standard library functions (malloc, free, pthread operations, string functions)\\n- Uses INTERCEPTOR macros to wrap libc functions\\n- Starts at line 311 with pthread_create and continues with numerous library function interceptors\\n- This runtime component captures memory operations at the libc level\\n\\n**2.
